			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"US Bank" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_the_United_States_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Bank of the United States (disambiguation)">Bank of the United States</a>.</div>

<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>U.S. Bancorp</b> (stylized as <b>us bancorp</b>) is an American <a href="/wiki/Bank_holding_company" title="Bank holding company">bank holding company</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a>, and incorporated in <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> It is the parent company of <b>U.S. Bank</b> National Association, and is on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_banks_in_the_United_States" title="List of largest banks in the United States">list of largest banks in the United States</a>. The company provides banking, investment, mortgage, trust, and payment services products to individuals, businesses, governmental entities, and other financial institutions. It has 3,106 <a href="/wiki/Branch_(banking)" title="Branch (banking)">branches</a> and 4,842 <a href="/wiki/Automated_teller_machine" title="Automated teller machine">ATMs</a>, primarily in the Western and Midwestern <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10K_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K-1">[1]</a></sup> It is ranked 117th on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The company also owns <a href="/wiki/Elavon" title="Elavon">Elavon</a>, a processor of credit card transactions for merchants and Elan Financial Services, a credit card issuer that issue credit card products to US Bank and other financial institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">U.S. Bancorp</caption><tbody><tr><td data-file-height="20"></a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-10K_1-0" class="reference"><a national charter, originally Charter #24, granted in 1863 following the passage of the <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_Act" title="National Bank Act">National Bank Act</a>. Earlier charters have expired as banks were closed or acquired, raising U.S. Bank's charter number from #24 to #2. The oldest national charter, originally granted to the <a href="/wiki/First_National_Bank_of_Philadelphia" class="mw-redirect" title="First National Bank of Philadelphia">First National Bank of Philadelphia</a>, is held by <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo" title="Wells Fargo">Wells Fargo</a>, which it obtained upon its merger with <a href="/wiki/Wachovia" title="Wachovia">Wachovia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Bancorp&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:214px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Usbank-stlouis.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1f/Usbank-stlouis.jpg" decoding="async" width="212" height="472" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="212" data-file-height="472"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 212px;height: 472px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1f/Usbank-stlouis.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="212" data-height="472" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Usbank-stlouis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One US Bank Plaza in downtown <a href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis, Missouri</a></div></div></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2008-0712-MPLS-pan00-mp-edit.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/2008-0712-MPLS-pan00-mp-edit.JPG/220px-2008-0712-MPLS-pan00-mp-edit.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2226"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 115px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/2008-0712-MPLS-pan00-mp-edit.JPG/220px-2008-0712-MPLS-pan00-mp-edit.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="115" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2008-0712-MPLS-pan00-mp-edit.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Downtown Minneapolis; U.S. Bancorp Center is the second unobstructed tower from the left.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HowardHannaUSBankHudsonOH.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/HowardHannaUSBankHudsonOH.JPG/220px-HowardHannaUSBankHudsonOH.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/HowardHannaUSBankHudsonOH.JPG/220px-HowardHannaUSBankHudsonOH.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HowardHannaUSBankHudsonOH.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>US Bank in <a href="/wiki/Hudson,_Ohio" title="Hudson, Ohio">Hudson, Ohio</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Bank_Tower_during_09_Finals.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/US_Bank_Tower_during_09_Finals.jpg/220px-US_Bank_Tower_during_09_Finals.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/US_Bank_Tower_during_09_Finals.jpg/220px-US_Bank_Tower_during_09_Finals.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Bank_Tower_during_09_Finals.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Tower_(Los_Angeles)" title="U.S. Bank Tower (Los Angeles)">US Bank Tower</a> in downtown <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles, California">Los Angeles, California</a></div></div></div>
<p>The U.S. Bank name first appeared as <b>United States National Bank of Portland</b>, established in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a>, in 1891.<sup id="cite_ref-richheritage_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richheritage-7">[7]</a></sup> It changed its name to the United States National Bank of Oregon in 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-richheritage_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richheritage-7">[7]</a></sup> In 1902, it merged with Ainsworth National Bank of Portland, but kept the U.S. National Bank name.<sup id="cite_ref-richheritage_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richheritage-7">[7]</a></sup></p><p>The central part of the franchise dates from 1864, with the formation of First National Bank of Minneapolis.<sup id="cite_ref-richheritage_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richheritage-7">[7]</a></sup> In 1929, that bank merged with First National Bank of St. Paul (also formed in 1864) and several smaller <a href="/wiki/Upper_Midwest" title="Upper Midwest">Upper Midwest</a> banks to form the First Bank Stock Corporation, which changed its name to <b><a href="/wiki/First_Bank_System" title="First Bank System">First Bank System</a></b> in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-richheritage_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richheritage-7">[7]</a></sup></p><p>In the eastern part of the franchise, Farmers and Millers Bank in Milwaukee opened its doors in 1853, growing into the First National Bank of Milwaukee and eventually becoming First Wisconsin and ultimately <a href="/wiki/Firstar_Corporation" title="Firstar Corporation">Firstar Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-richheritage_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richheritage-7">[7]</a></sup> In Cincinnati, First National Bank of Cincinnati opened for business in 1863 under National Charter #24—the charter that U.S. Bancorp still operates under today, and one of the oldest active national bank charters in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-richheritage_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richheritage-7">[7]</a></sup> Despite having started up in the midst of the Civil War, First National Bank of Cincinnati went on to survive many decades to grow into <a href="/wiki/Star_Banc_Corporation" title="Star Banc Corporation">Star Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-richheritage_7-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-richheritage-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._Bancorp_of_Oregon_era">U.S. Bancorp of Oregon era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Bancorp&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: U.S. Bancorp of Oregon era" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>U.S. Bancorp of Oregon officially became a banking holding company for the U.S. National Bank of Oregon in January 1969<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1969jan06_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1969jan06-8">[8]</a></sup> after receiving authorization from its bank directors on September 9, 1968<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1968sep09_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1968sep09-9">[9]</a></sup> and subsequently receiving legal approval to proceed from the <a href="/wiki/Comptroller_of_the_Currency" class="mw-redirect" title="Comptroller of the Currency">Comptroller of the Currency</a> on November 28, 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1968nov29_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1968nov29-10">[10]</a></sup> LeRoy B. Staver, president and chief executive officer of the bank, was quickly appointed chairman and chief executive officer for the new holding company while Robert B. Wilson was appointed president of the holding company and also executive vice president for the bank.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1969feb25_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1969feb25-11">[11]</a></sup> Wilson later resign as president in December 1972<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1972dec26_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1972dec26-12">[12]</a></sup> and his position was filled eight months later by John A. Elorriaga.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1973aug28_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1973aug28-13">[13]</a></sup></p><p>After a long period of service, Staver finally retired in October 1974 and was succeeded by John Elorriaga who was promoted to chairman and chief executive officer while Carl W. Mays Jr was named president in Elorriaga's place.<sup id="cite_ref-lat-1974oct29_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-1974oct29-14">[14]</a></sup></p><p>A major change in the organization of leadership in U.S. Bancorp of Oregon occurred in August 1983. Although Elorriaga remained as chairman and chief executive officer for the firm, Mays was appointed to the new position of executive assistant to the chairman while Edmund P. Jensen was appointed president as replacement to Mays, and Roger L. Breezley was appointed to the new post of chief operating officer.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1983aug30_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1983aug30-15">[15]</a></sup></p><p>In December 1986, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Forest_Grove,_Oregon" title="Forest Grove, Oregon">Forest Grove, Oregon</a>-based Valley National Corporation (not to be confused with the Phoenix, Arizona, company of the same name) with its five-branch Valley National Bank of Forest Grove subsidiary for $13.7 million in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1986dec08_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1986dec08-16">[16]</a></sup></p><p>U.S. Bancorp of Oregon made its first acquisition outside the state of Oregon by announcing in December 1986 the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Spokane,_Washington" title="Spokane, Washington">Spokane, Washington</a>-based Old National Bancorp with its Old National Bank of Washington and First National Bank of Spokane subsidiaries for $174 million.<sup id="cite_ref-spi-1986dec18_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spi-1986dec18-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-st-1986dec18_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-st-1986dec18-18">[18]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in July 1987 on the first day that the state of Washington had allowed bank acquisitions by out-of-state companies.<sup id="cite_ref-st-1987jun30_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-st-1987jun30-19">[19]</a></sup></p><p>In December 1986, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Camas,_Washington" title="Camas, Washington">Camas, Washington</a>-based Heritage Bank for $2.8 million.<sup id="cite_ref-lat-1986dec25_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-1986dec25-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spi-1986dec25_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spi-1986dec25-21">[21]</a></sup></p><p>In May 1987, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Seattle,_Washington" class="mw-redirect" title="Seattle, Washington">Seattle, Washington</a>-based Peoples Bancorp with its Peoples National Bank subsidiary for $275 million in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-1987may20_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-1987may20-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-st-1987may19_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-st-1987may19-23">[23]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in December 1987.<sup id="cite_ref-spi-1988jan01_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spi-1988jan01-24">[24]</a></sup> After the acquisition, Peoples and Old National were combined to form U.S. Bank of Washington.
</p><p>John Elorriaga retired as chairman of the board and chief executive officer in November 1987 and was replaced by Roger L. Breezley while Jensen continuef as president.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1987oct27_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1987oct27-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spi-1987nov02_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spi-1987nov02-26">[26]</a></sup></p><p>In December 1987, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Bellingham,_Washington" title="Bellingham, Washington">Bellingham, Washington</a>-based Mt Baker Bank for $25 million.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1987dec17_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1987dec17-27">[27]</a></sup></p><p>U.S. Bancorp of Oregon entered the state of <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> by announcing in April 1988 the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Eureka,_California" title="Eureka, California">Eureka, California</a>-based Bank of Loleta with seven branch offices in <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_County,_California" title="Humboldt County, California">Humboldt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Del_Norte_County,_California" title="Del Norte County, California">Del Norte</a> counties for $15.3 million in cash.<sup id="cite_ref-to-1988apr09_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to-1988apr09-28">[28]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in December 1988 and was renamed U.S. Bank of California.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-1989jun12_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-1989jun12-29">[29]</a></sup></p><p>In April 1988, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Bellingham,_Washington" title="Bellingham, Washington">Bellingham, Washington</a>-based Northwestern Commercial Bank for $15.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1988apr28_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1988apr28-30">[30]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in November 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-1988nov17_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-1988nov17-31">[31]</a></sup></p><p>In July 1988, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Auburn,_Washington" title="Auburn, Washington">Auburn, Washington</a>-based Western Independent Bancshares with its Auburn Valley Bank subsidiary for $4.25 million in cash.<sup id="cite_ref-spi-1988jul23_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spi-1988jul23-32">[32]</a></sup></p><p>In October 1989, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento, California</a>-based Mother Lode Savings Bank with three branch offices for $5.3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-to-1989oct19_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to-1989oct19-33">[33]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in August 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-to-1990aug26_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to-1990aug26-34">[34]</a></sup> This acquisition was one of the first of a thrift by a commercial bank in the nation since legislation permitting such takeovers went into effect.
</p><p>During the late 1980s, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon made several attempts to enter the state of Idaho by the acquisition of an existing Idaho-based bank, the only method then allowed under Idaho law, but failed when the price got too high.<sup id="cite_ref-sfc-1991jul29_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sfc-1991jul29-35">[35]</a></sup> In March 1990, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced that they would established a bank through a loophole in Federal banking law that allow the Office of the Comptroller of the Currency to allow the relocation of bank headquarters within 30 miles of their present location without regards to state boundaries and state regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-1990mar13_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-1990mar13-36">[36]</a></sup> So U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced that they plan to transfer the existing branches of the First National Bank of Spokane to the U.S. Bancorp of Washington and then ask permission from the Office of the Comptroller of the Currency to move the headquarters of First National from Spokane, Washington, to <a href="/wiki/Coeur_d%27Alene,_Idaho" title="Coeur d'Alene, Idaho">Coeur d'Alene, Idaho</a>. After receiving Federal approval, First National was finally moved in February 1992 and renamed U.S. Bank of Idaho.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-1992feb19_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-1992feb19-37">[37]</a></sup></p><p>In July 1990, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Auburn,_California" title="Auburn, California">Auburn, California</a>-based HeartFed Financial Corporation with its Heart Federal Savings and Loan subsidiary for $107.8 million in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-to-1990jul18_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to-1990jul18-38">[38]</a></sup> At the time of the announcement, Heart Federal Savings had 29 branch offices in northern California. The acquisition was completed in March 1991 for $118 million.<sup id="cite_ref-upi-1991mar28_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upi-1991mar28-39">[39]</a></sup></p><p>In November 1991, Edmund P. Jensen was given the post of chief operating officer in addition to his duties as president, making him a possible successor to Breezley.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1991nov05_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1991nov05-40">[40]</a></sup></p><p>In February 1992, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the 20 branch offices in <a href="/wiki/Northern_California" title="Northern California">Northern California</a> and 29 branch offices in <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a> for $70 million that were being divested by <a href="/wiki/Bankamerica_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Bankamerica Corporation">Bankamerica Corporation</a> as a result of Bank of America's impending acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Security_Pacific_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Security Pacific Corporation">Security Pacific Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lat-1992feb27_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-1992feb27-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sb-1992feb27_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sb-1992feb27-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prn-1992feb27_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-1992feb27-43">[43]</a></sup> This acquisition gave U.S. Bancorp of Oregon its first presence in the state of Nevada.
</p><p>Another major change in the organization of leadership in U.S. Bancorp of Oregon occurred in January 1993. While retaining his position as chief operating officer, Edmund P. Jensen was appointed vice chairman while giving his position of president to Kevin R. Kelly. At the same time, Gerry B. Cameron was appointed vice chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-1993jan14_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-1993jan14-44">[44]</a></sup> Ten months later, Jensen resigned to become president of <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa Inc.</a><sup id="cite_ref-nyt-1993oct27_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-1993oct27-45">[45]</a></sup> In January 1994, Gerry Cameron was first appointed chief operating officer as a replacement to Jensen<sup id="cite_ref-prn-1994jan06_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-1994jan06-46">[46]</a></sup> and later appointed chief executive officer just three weeks later.<sup id="cite_ref-to-1994jan27_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to-1994jan27-47">[47]</a></sup> Kelly submitted his resignation as president in March 1994<sup id="cite_ref-to-1994mar19_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to-1994mar19-48">[48]</a></sup> and Breezley finally gave up the chairmanship to Cameron in April 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-1994apr20_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-1994apr20-49">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-st-1994apr20_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-st-1994apr20-50">[50]</a></sup></p><p>In May 1995, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Boise,_Idaho" title="Boise, Idaho">Boise, Idaho</a>-based West One Bancorp for $1.8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-to-1995may09_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to-1995may09-52">[52]</a></sup> At the time of the announcement, West One had branch offices in Idaho, Oregon, Washington, and Utah while U.S. Bancorp of Oregon had branch offices in Oregon, Washington, California, Idaho, and Nevada. The acquisition was completed in December 1995 and gave U.S. Bancorp of Oregon its first entry into the state of Utah.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> As part of the acquisition deal, West One's chairman and chief executive Daniel R. Nelson would become the chief operating officer and president of U.S. Bancorp and he would later be Cameron's successor as chairman and CEO upon Cameron's planned retirement in three years. Since both U.S. Bancorp and West One had overlapping territories in Oregon and Washington, the U.S. Justice Department would only allow the acquisition to proceed if U.S. Bancorp would sell off 27 branch offices in Washington and Oregon.<sup id="cite_ref-tsr-1995dec12_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tsr-1995dec12-54">[54]</a></sup> As a result of the regulatory ruling, U.S. Bancorp sold 25 branch offices in Oregon, four in central Washington and one in Idaho to <a href="/wiki/First_Hawaiian_Bank" title="First Hawaiian Bank">First Hawaiian Bank</a> for $38 million in cash.<sup id="cite_ref-st-1995dec05_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-st-1995dec05-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tsr-1995dec05_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tsr-1995dec05-56">[56]</a></sup></p><p>In February 1996, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/San_Ramon,_California" title="San Ramon, California">San Ramon, California</a>-based California Bancshares for $309 million in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-lat-1996feb13_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-1996feb13-57">[57]</a></sup> California Bancshares had a total of 38 branches in the East San Francisco Bay Area in nine separate banks that included Alameda First National, Community First National, Modesto Banking Co., Commercial Bank of Fremont, Lamorinda National Bank, Bank of San Ramon Valley, Westside Bank, Concord Commercial Bank and Bank of Milipitas. The acquisition was completed in June 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-upi-1996jun06_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upi-1996jun06-58">[58]</a></sup></p><p>In September 1996, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/St._George,_Utah" title="St. George, Utah">St. George, Utah</a>-based Sun Capital Bancorp with its three-branch office Sun Capital Bank subsidiary for $15.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-dn-1996sep26_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dn-1996sep26-59">[59]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in January 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-slt-1997jan04_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slt-1997jan04-60">[60]</a></sup></p><p>In December 1996, Daniel R. Nelson, president and chief operating officer of U.S. Bancorp of Oregon, unexpectedly announced his early retirement effective on New Year’s Day 1997. Nelson was originally in line to be Gerry B. Cameron's successor as chairman and chief executive upon the Cameron's planned retirement on New Year's Day 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-tsr-1996dec25_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tsr-1996dec25-61">[61]</a></sup></p><p>In December 1996, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento, California</a>-based Business &amp; Professional Bank for $35 million in cash.<sup id="cite_ref-to-1996dec28_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to-1996dec28-62">[62]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in May 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-prn-1997may01_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-1997may01-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Bank_System_era">First Bank System era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Bancorp&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: First Bank System era" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:97px;"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Bank_logo_1979.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/73/First_Bank_logo_1979.JPG" decoding="async" width="95" height="87" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="95" data-file-height="87"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 95px;height: 87px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/7/73/First_Bank_logo_1979.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="95" data-height="87" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:First_Bank_logo_1979.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>First Bank System used this logo from 1979. It incorporates the silhouette of the number one.</div></div></div>
<p>In March 1997, the <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis" title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a>-based First Bank System announced the pending acquisition of the Portland, Oregon-based U.S. Bancorp of Oregon for $9 billion in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ct-1997mar20_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct-1997mar20-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tsr-1997mar21_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tsr-1997mar21-66">[66]</a></sup> At the time of the announcement, U.S. Bancorp of Oregon had banking offices in Oregon, Washington, California, Idaho and Utah while First Bank System had banking offices in Minnesota, Colorado, Nebraska, North Dakota, South Dakota, Montana, Iowa, Illinois, Wisconsin, Kansas, and Wyoming.  Under the terms of the acquisition, First Bank System would be renamed U.S. Bancorp with the headquarters for the newly combined company being at First Bank's existing headquarters in Minneapolis. <a href="/wiki/John_F._Grundhofer" title="John F. Grundhofer">John F. Grundhofer</a>, chairman and chief executive of First Bank, was appointed president and chief executive of the new company while Gerry B. Cameron, chairman and chief executive of U.S. Bancorp of Oregon, was appointed chairman of the new company, which he held until his retirement in 1998. The acquisition was completed in August 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-mst-1997aug02_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mst-1997aug02-67">[67]</a></sup> Approximately 4000 jobs were eliminated, mostly in Portland.<sup id="cite_ref-to-1997aug02_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to-1997aug02-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Brief_history_of_First_Bank_prior_to_acquisition">Brief history of First Bank prior to acquisition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Bancorp&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Brief history of First Bank prior to acquisition" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/First_Bank_System" title="First Bank System">First Bank System</a></div>
<p>First Bank System can trace its roots back to the formation of First National Bank of Minneapolis in 1864. In 1929, the First National Bank of Minneapolis joined together with the First National Bank of St. Paul to form a joint holding company for both banks that was called the First Bank Stock Corporation while keep both subsidiary banks legally separate. The new holding company quickly grew by acquiring other banks in four state region before the <a href="/wiki/Bank_Holding_Company_Act_of_1956" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank Holding Company Act of 1956">Bank Holding Company Act of 1956</a> prohibited such actions. First Bank Stock Corporation was renamed First Bank Stock Corporation Inc. in 1968.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._Bancorp_after_takeover_by_First_Bank_System">U.S. Bancorp after takeover by First Bank System</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Bancorp&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: U.S. Bancorp after takeover by First Bank System" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In September 1997, the new U.S. Bancorp, formerly First Bank System, announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/St._Cloud,_Minnesota" title="St. Cloud, Minnesota">St. Cloud, Minnesota</a>-based Zappco, Inc. with its three banks and six banking locations for an undisclosed amount.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> At the time of the announcement, U.S. Bancorp had more than 1,000 banking offices in the states of Minnesota, Oregon, Washington, Colorado, California, Idaho, Nebraska, North Dakota, Nevada, South Dakota, Montana, Iowa, Illinois, Utah, Wisconsin, Kansas, and Wyoming. The acquisition was completed in December 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-mst-1997dec16_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mst-1997dec16-70">[70]</a></sup></p><p>In March 1998, U.S. Bancorp announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Vancouver,_Washington" title="Vancouver, Washington">Vancouver, Washington</a>-based Northwest Bancshares with its 10-branch offices Northwest National Bank subsidiary for an undisclosed amount.<sup id="cite_ref-tsr-1998mar14_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tsr-1998mar14-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mspbj-1998mar13_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mspbj-1998mar13-72">[72]</a></sup> In October 1998, the U.S. Justice Department agreed to allow the acquisition to proceed on the condition that one of the Northwest National Bank branch offices was to be sold.<sup id="cite_ref-spi-1998oct10_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spi-1998oct10-73">[73]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in December 1998 after U.S. Bancorp sold the request banking office to Centennial Bank of Eugene.<sup id="cite_ref-tc-1998dec16_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tc-1998dec16-74">[74]</a></sup></p><p>At the end of 1998, Gerry Cameron retired as chairman and handed the position over to John Grundhofer who added the title of chairman to his other positions of president and chief executive officer.<sup id="cite_ref-sppp-1998dec24_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sppp-1998dec24-75">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mst-1998dec29_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mst-1998dec29-76">[76]</a></sup></p><p>In February 1999, U.S. Bancorp announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a>-based Bank of Commerce with its 10 branch offices for $314 million in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-mst-1999feb19_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mst-1999feb19-77">[77]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lat-1999feb19_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-1999feb19-78">[78]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt-1999feb20_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-1999feb20-79">[79]</a></sup> The acquisition was finalized in July 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-mspbj-1999jul19_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mspbj-1999jul19-80">[80]</a></sup></p><p>In May 1999, U.S. Bancorp announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Newport_Beach,_California" title="Newport Beach, California">Newport Beach, California</a>-based Western Bancorp with its Santa Monica Bank and Southern California Bank subsidiaries and a total of 31 branch offices for $904 million in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt-1999may20_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-1999may20-82">[82]</a></sup> At the time of the announcement, U.S. Bancorp had 98 branch offices within California. The acquisition was finalized in November 1999 for $1.04 billion in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-lat-1999nov17_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-1999nov17-83">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prn-1999nov16_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-1999nov16-84">[84]</a></sup></p><p>In July 1999, Philip G. Heasley was appointed president and chief operating officer of U.S. Bancorp. John Grundhofer had handed over the position of president to Heasley while still retaining the titles of chairman and chief executive officer.<sup id="cite_ref-mst-1999jul22_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mst-1999jul22-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prn-1999jul21_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-1999jul21-86">[86]</a></sup> Heasley had assisted Grundhofer in turning the company around from near insolvency when the company was originally known as First Bank until it became a successful financial institution that became large enough to be absorb other banks, including U.S. Bancorp of Oregon in 1997. Heasley resigned the following year to join <a href="/wiki/Bank_One" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank One">Bank One</a> as the head of their <a href="/wiki/First_USA" class="mw-redirect" title="First USA">First USA</a> credit card unit<sup id="cite_ref-ct-2000nov08_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct-2000nov08-87">[87]</a></sup> around the same time Firstar was about to takeover U.S. Bancorp.
</p><p>In September 1999, U.S. Bancorp announced the pending acquisition of the San Diego-based Peninsula Bank with its 11 branch offices for $104 million in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-1999sep03_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-1999sep03-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lat-1999sep03_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-1999sep03-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mst-1999sep03_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mst-1999sep03-90">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sdut-1999sep03_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sdut-1999sep03-91">[91]</a></sup> In early January 2000, a group of Peninsula Bank stockholders tried to stop the merger because the initial merger agreement was made prior to the huge 27% single-day drop in the value of U.S. Bancorp stock which effectively lowered the purchase price.<sup id="cite_ref-sdut-2000jan07_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sdut-2000jan07-92">[92]</a></sup> The acquisition was later completed in January 2000 at a 10% reduction of the original price negotiated.<sup id="cite_ref-sdut-2000jan19_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sdut-2000jan19-93">[93]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2000, U.S. Bancorp announced the acquisition of the San Diego-based Scripps Financial Corporation with its nine-branch office Scripps Bank subsidiary for $155 million in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-prn-2000jun27_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-2000jun27-94">[94]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in October 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-prn-2000oct13_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-2000oct13-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Firstar_era">Firstar era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Bancorp&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Firstar era" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In October 2000, <a href="/wiki/Firstar_Corporation" title="Firstar Corporation">Firstar Corporation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee,_Wisconsin" class="mw-redirect" title="Milwaukee, Wisconsin">Milwaukee, Wisconsin</a>, announced the pending acquisition of U.S. Bancorp of <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis,_Minnesota" class="mw-redirect" title="Minneapolis, Minnesota">Minneapolis, Minnesota</a>, for $21 billion in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-2000oct05_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-2000oct05-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prn-2000oct04_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-2000oct04-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lat-2000oct05_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-2000oct05-98">[98]</a></sup> Firstar completed its buyout of U.S. Bancorp on February 27, 2001, and changed its name to U.S. Bancorp.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Under the merger agreement, <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Grundhofer" title="Jerry Grundhofer">Jerry Grundhofer</a>, president and chief executive officer of Firstar, would continue in those positions in the combined company while his older brother, <a href="/wiki/John_Grundhofer" class="mw-redirect" title="John Grundhofer">John Grundhofer</a>, chairman, president and chief executive officer of U.S. Bancorp, would serve as chairman of the board in the combined company until his planned retirement on December 31, 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-lat-2000oct05_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-2000oct05-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mst-2001feb27_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mst-2001feb27-100">[100]</a></sup> Though some administrative functions would remain in Milwaukee and Cincinnati, it was decided that the new combined company would be based in Minneapolis and that the new company would use the U.S. Bancorp name.
</p><p>To allow the merger to proceed, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">U.S. Department of Justice</a> required Firstar to sell 11 branch offices in the Minneapolis-area and 2 in <a href="/wiki/Council_Bluffs,_Iowa" title="Council Bluffs, Iowa">Council Bluffs, Iowa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bremer_Bank" title="Bremer Bank">Bremer Bank</a> of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Paul,_Minnesota" title="Saint Paul, Minnesota">Saint Paul, Minnesota</a>, purchased the 11 Minneapolis-area Firstar offices<sup id="cite_ref-mspbj-2001jan31_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mspbj-2001jan31-102">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mst-2001feb01_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mst-2001feb01-103">[103]</a></sup> while Liberty Bank of <a href="/wiki/West_Des_Moines,_Iowa" title="West Des Moines, Iowa">West Des Moines, Iowa</a>, purchased the 2 Council Bluffs offices.<sup id="cite_ref-cbj-2001feb06_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbj-2001feb06-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-owh-2001feb06_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-owh-2001feb06-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Brief_history_of_Firstar_prior_to_acquisition">Brief history of Firstar prior to acquisition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Bancorp&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Brief history of Firstar prior to acquisition" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Firstar_Corporation" title="Firstar Corporation">Firstar Corporation</a></div>
<p>Although the origin of the Milwaukee-based Firstar Corporation can be traced back to the founding of the Farmer's and Millers Bank in Milwaukee in 1853 and the later formation of the First Wisconsin National Bank in 1919, the actual company that took over U.S. Bancorp in 2001 is the actually the same company and leadership that was responsible for the takeover of Firstar 27 months earlier in 1998, namely <a href="/wiki/Star_Banc_Corporation" title="Star Banc Corporation">Star Banc Corporation</a>. That bank, in turn, traced its roots to the founding of First National Bank of Cincinnati in 1863. Jerry Grundhofer and his team from Star Banc were instrumental in both acquisitions.
</p><p>Present-day U.S. Bancorp retains Star Banc's pre-1998 stock price history, and as mentioned above operates under the charter originally granted to First National Bank of Cincinnati. Additionally, all SEC filings before 1998 are under Star Banc, and all filings from 1998 to 2000 are under Firstar.
</p>
<h4 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._Bancorp_after_takeover_by_Firstar">U.S. Bancorp after takeover by Firstar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Bancorp&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: U.S. Bancorp after takeover by Firstar" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h4>
<p>In April 2001, the new U.S. Bancorp announced the pending acquisition of all 20 branch offices in California of the <a href="/wiki/Encino,_Los_Angeles" title="Encino, Los Angeles">Encino</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Century_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Century Bank">Pacific Century Bank</a> from its <a href="/wiki/Honolulu" title="Honolulu">Honolulu</a>-based parent <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Century_Financial_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Century Financial Corporation">Pacific Century Financial Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lat-2001apr24_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lat-2001apr24-106">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prn-2001jun05_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-2001jun05-107">[107]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in September 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-prn-2001sep10_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-2001sep10-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pbn-2001sep10_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pbn-2001sep10-109">[109]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2002, U.S. Bancorp announced the pending acquisition of all 57 retail banking branches of the <a href="/wiki/San_Mateo,_California" title="San Mateo, California">San Mateo, California</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Bay_View_Bank" title="Bay View Bank">Bay View Bank</a> from its <a href="/wiki/Bay_View_Capital_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay View Capital Corporation">Bay View Capital Corporation</a> parent for $429 million.<sup id="cite_ref-sfbt-2002jul22_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sfbt-2002jul22-110">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-prn-2002jul22_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-2002jul22-111">[111]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in November 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-prn-2002nov01_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prn-2002nov01-112">[112]</a></sup></p><p>On New Years Day 2003, John Grundhofer retired as chairman of U.S. Bancorp and handed the position to his younger brother Jerry Grundhofer, who added the title of chairman to his other positions of president and chief executive officer in the corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-mbj-2002dec18_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mbj-2002dec18-113">[113]</a></sup></p><p>In May 2004, U.S. Bancorp announced that it was acquiring the $34 billion corporate trust bond administration business from <a href="/wiki/National_City_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="National City Corporation">National City Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2004may25_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2004may25-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cbf-2004may25_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbf-2004may25-115">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bw-2004oct19_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2004oct19-116">[116]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2004, <a href="/wiki/Richard_K._Davis" title="Richard K. Davis">Richard K. Davis</a> was appointed chief operating officer and president of U.S. Bancorp. Jerry Grundhofer had handed over the position of president to Davis while still retaining the titles of chairman and chief executive officer.<sup id="cite_ref-mspbj-2004oct19_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mspbj-2004oct19-117">[117]</a></sup> Davis had been a protege of Grundhofer since their days together at Star Banc Corporation and had assisted in the takeover of Firstar by Star Banc in 1998<sup id="cite_ref-ce-1998jul02_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ce-1998jul02-118">[118]</a></sup> and the later acquisition of U.S. Bancorp by Firstar in 2001.
</p><p>In November 2005, U.S. Bancorp announced that it was acquiring the $410 billion corporate trust and institutional custody businesses of <a href="/wiki/Wachovia_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Wachovia Corporation">Wachovia Corporation</a> for $720 million in cash.<sup id="cite_ref-mspbj-2005nov29_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mspbj-2005nov29-119">[119]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2006, U.S. Bancorp announced that it was acquiring the $123 billion municipal and corporate bond trustee business from <a href="/wiki/SunTrust" class="mw-redirect" title="SunTrust">SunTrust</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2006jul25_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2006jul25-120">[120]</a></sup></p><p>In June 2006, U.S. Bancorp announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Avon,_Colorado" title="Avon, Colorado">Avon, Colorado</a>-based Vail Banks Inc. with its WestStar Bank subsidiary and 23 locations for $98.6 million in cash.<sup id="cite_ref-mspbj-2006jun01_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mspbj-2006jun01-121">[121]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in September 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2006sep01_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2006sep01-122">[122]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2006, U.S. Bancorp announced that it was acquiring the $30 billion municipal bond trustee business from <a href="/wiki/LaSalle_Bank" title="LaSalle Bank">LaSalle Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2006nov10_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2006nov10-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mspbj-2006nov10_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mspbj-2006nov10-124">[124]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2006, U.S. Bancorp announced the pending acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Falls,_Montana" title="Great Falls, Montana">Great Falls, Montana</a>-based United Financial Corporation with its Heritage Bank subsidiary for $71 million in stock.<sup id="cite_ref-slbj-2006nov07_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slbj-2006nov07-125">[125]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in February 2007 and nearly double the branch presence of U.S. Bank in Montana.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2007feb07_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2007feb07-126">[126]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2006, Jerry Grundhofer handed over the position of chief executive officer to president Richard Davis while Grundhofer remained chairman until his retirement the following year in December 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2006jul18_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2006jul18-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mspbj-2006jul18_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mspbj-2006jul18-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sppp-2006dec13_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sppp-2006dec13-129">[129]</a></sup> After Grundhofer retirement in December 2007, Davis added the position of chairman to his other titles of president and chief executive officer.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2007dec11_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2007dec11-130">[130]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2008, the U.S. Bancorp announced the pending acquisition of the seven-office Los Angeles-based Mellon 1st Business Bank from the <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_New_York_Mellon" class="mw-redirect" title="Bank of New York Mellon">Bank of New York Mellon</a> for an undisclosed amount in cash.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2008mar28_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2008mar28-131">[131]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in June 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt-2008jun03_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-2008jun03-132">[132]</a></sup></p><p>On November 14, 2008, the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Treasury" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Treasury">U.S. Treasury</a> invested $6,599,000,000 in preferred stock and warrants in the company via the <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Economic_Stabilization_Act_of_2008" title="Emergency Economic Stabilization Act of 2008">Emergency Economic Stabilization Act of 2008</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p><p>On November 21, 2008, the company acquired the failed Downey Savings &amp; Loan Association and also the failed Pomona First Federal Bancorp in a transaction facilitated by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Deposit_Insurance_Corporation" title="Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation">Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation</a> for an undisclosed amount.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> Downey Savings had 170 branch offices in California and five branch offices in Arizona while PFF Bank had 38 branch offices in Southern California.
</p><p>In April 2009, U.S. Bancorp acquired the assets and deposits of the failed <a href="/wiki/Ketchum,_Idaho" title="Ketchum, Idaho">Ketchum, Idaho</a>-based First Bank of Idaho in a transaction facilitated by the FDIC.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2009apr24_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2009apr24-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-to-2009apr26_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-to-2009apr26-136">[136]</a></sup> First Bank of Idaho had seven offices in Idaho and Wyoming, some of which operated under the name First Bank of the Tetons.
</p><p>On June 17, 2009, the company redeemed the $6.6 billion of preferred stock and on July 15, 2009, it completed the purchase of a warrant held by the U.S. Treasury Department. This effectively concluded U.S. Bancorp’s participation in the <a href="/wiki/Capital_Purchase_Program" title="Capital Purchase Program">Capital Purchase Program</a>. It was the first bank to repay the <a href="/wiki/Troubled_Asset_Relief_Program" title="Troubled Asset Relief Program">Troubled Asset Relief Program</a> (TARP) funds.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p><p>On October 5, 2009, the company announced its acquisition of the $8 billion mutual fund administration and accounting servicing division of Fiduciary Management, Inc. for an undisclosed amount.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mjs-2009oct05_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mjs-2009oct05-139">[139]</a></sup></p><p>On October 7, 2009, the company agreed to buy the bond trustee business of First Citizens Bank, a subsidiary of <a href="/wiki/First_Citizens_BancShares" title="First Citizens BancShares">First Citizens BancShares</a> Inc. for an undisclosed amount.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bw-2009oct07_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2009oct07-141">[141]</a></sup></p><p>On October 20, 2009, the company completed a transaction to purchase the failed <a href="/wiki/FBOP_Corporation" title="FBOP Corporation">FBOP Corporation</a>'s nine subsidiary banks from the FDIC for an undisclosed amount. The banks included BankUSA, National Association with 2 offices in Arizona, <a href="/wiki/Cal_National_Bank" title="Cal National Bank">Cal National Bank</a> with 68 offices in California, Citizens National Bank with 1 office in Texas, Community Bank of Lemont with 1 office in Illinois, Madisonville State Bank with 1 office in Texas, North Houston Bank with 1 office in Texas, Pacific National Bank with 17 offices in California, Park National Bank with 31 offices in Illinois, and San Diego National Bank with 28 offices in California.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2009oct30_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2009oct30-142">[142]</a></sup></p><p>Since the company did not have a previous presence in Texas nor want one in the near future, the company subsequently sold the three banks in Texas in 2010 to Houston-based <a href="/wiki/Prosperity_Bancshares" title="Prosperity Bancshares">Prosperity Bancshares</a> for an undisclosed amount.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Each of the banks had one office each.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2009oct30_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2009oct30-142">[142]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2009, BB&amp;T Corporation (now <a href="/wiki/Truist_Financial" title="Truist Financial">Truist Financial</a>) announced the pending sale of its Nevada banking operations to U.S. Bancorp for an undisclosed amount. BB&amp;T had just acquired the 21 offices in Nevada through a transaction facilitated by the FDIC for disposal of the assets and deposits of the failed Alabama-based <a href="/wiki/Colonial_BancGroup" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonial BancGroup">Colonial BancGroup</a> but BB&amp;T had no desire to expand west of Texas while it wanted to keep the other Colonial former locations in the Southeastern United States.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj-2009oct15_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-2009oct15-144">[144]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in January 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2010jan19_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2010jan19-145">[145]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2010, U.S. Bancorp sold its <a href="/wiki/FAF_Advisors" class="mw-redirect" title="FAF Advisors">FAF Advisors</a> subsidiary to <a href="/wiki/Nuveen_Investments" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuveen Investments">Nuveen Investments</a> for $80 million and a 9.5% stake in Nuveen.<sup id="cite_ref-ccb-2010jul29_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccb-2010jul29-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mst-2010jul29_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mst-2010jul29-147">[147]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2011, U.S. Bancorp acquired the assets and deposits of the failed First Community Bank of New Mexico in a transaction facilitated by the FDIC for an asset discount of approximately $380 million.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> The acquisition had included 35 offices in New Mexico and 3 offices in Arizona.
</p><p>In January 2012, the company acquired the assets and deposits of the failed <a href="/wiki/Knoxville,_Tennessee" title="Knoxville, Tennessee">Knoxville, Tennessee</a>-based BankEast in a transaction facilitated by the FDIC for an asset discount of approximately $67.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> The acquisition had included 10 offices in the Knoxville area.
</p><p>In December 2012, it was announced that U.S. Bank will offer <a href="/wiki/Mitek_Systems" title="Mitek Systems">Mitek</a>'s Mobile Photo Bill Pay product to its customers in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2013, U.S. Bancorp announced that it was acquiring the $57 billion municipal bond trustee business from <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mst-2013mar19_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mst-2013mar19-151">[151]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2014, U.S. Bancorp announced the pending acquisition of 94 branch offices of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_One_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter One Bank">Charter One Bank</a> in Chicago from the <a href="/wiki/Citizens_Financial_Group" title="Citizens Financial Group">RBS Citizens Financial Group</a> for $315 million,<sup id="cite_ref-cdb-2014jan07_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cdb-2014jan07-152">[152]</a></sup> doubling its market share in Chicago.<sup id="cite_ref-ct-201jun23_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct-201jun23-153">[153]</a></sup> 13 Charter One branches were closed due to their close proximity to existing U.S. Bank offices.<sup id="cite_ref-ccb-2014apr29_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccb-2014apr29-154">[154]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed in June 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-ct-201jun23_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ct-201jun23-153">[153]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2015, chief financial officer Andrew Cecere was promoted to chief operating officer.<sup id="cite_ref-mspbj-2015jan20_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mspbj-2015jan20-155">[155]</a></sup> A year later, Cecere was given the additional position of president.<sup id="cite_ref-bw-2016jan19_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bw-2016jan19-156">[156]</a></sup></p><p>In January 2017, U.S. Bancorp announced that chairman and CEO Richard Davis was going to hand over his CEO position to president and COO Andrew Cecere in April 2017 while still remaining chairman of the corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-sppp-2017jan17_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sppp-2017jan17-157">[157]</a></sup> Davis officially retired from the company in April 2018 and handed over the chairmanship position to Cecere.<sup id="cite_ref-tcbm-2018jan18_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcbm-2018jan18-158">[158]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2018, the bank was charged by the Department of Justice with failing to implement measures preventing illegal activities, including one case of abetting them.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-159">[159]</a></sup> To defer prosecution, U.S. Bancorp agreed to pay $613 million in fines and agreed to implement measures to show the authorities that it had improved the monitoring of its customer transactions.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-159">[159]</a></sup>  $505 million was distributed in September 2018 to customers of an illegal payday loan business whose suspicious activities US Bancorp had failed to report.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p><p>In December 2019, the bank dismissed Emily James, a Portland, Ore., call-center employee, and her supervisor, after James personally gave $20 of her own money to a customer in need, Marc Eugenio. On Christmas Eve, Eugenio ran out of gasoline and cash, and he was stranded at a gas station when his U.S. Bank debit card was rejected because funds he had deposited two days earlier had not yet been released into his account as he had been promised. After an unsuccessful attempt to release the funds, James met Eugenio at the gas station during her break and offered him $20 from her own pocket as a Christmas Eve act of kindness. She was fired from her job, despite U.S. Bankcorp's policy that "Our employees are empowered to do the right thing."<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view"><span title="Comment: {{{1}}}">POV?</span></a> <span class="metadata"> – <a href="/wiki/Talk:U.S._Bancorp" title="Talk:U.S. Bancorp">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> After Nicolas Kristof published a critique of the firing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> the bank agreed to rehire the employees.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_corporate_buildings">Notable corporate buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Bancorp&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Notable corporate buildings" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Center_(Phoenix)" title="U.S. Bank Center (Phoenix)">U.S. Bank Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Tower_(Sacramento)" title="U.S. Bank Tower (Sacramento)">U.S. Bank Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sacramento,_California" title="Sacramento, California">Sacramento, California</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/One_California" title="One California">One California</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Francisco, California">San Francisco, California</a>, sports the U.S. Bank logo and houses bank offices</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Tower_(Los_Angeles)" title="U.S. Bank Tower (Los Angeles)">U.S. Bank Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles, California">Los Angeles, California</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_tallest_buildings_in_the_United_States" title="List of tallest buildings in the United States">third tallest building</a> west of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Tower_(Denver)" title="U.S. Bank Tower (Denver)">U.S. Bank Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Denver,_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Denver, Colorado">Denver, Colorado</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Plaza_(Boise)" title="U.S. Bank Plaza (Boise)">U.S. Bank Plaza</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boise,_Idaho" title="Boise, Idaho">Boise, Idaho</a></li>
<li>U.S. Bank Building in <a href="/wiki/Chicago,_Illinois" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago, Illinois">Chicago, Illinois</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Bank_Building_(Davenport,_Iowa)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="U.S. Bank Building (Davenport, Iowa) (page does not exist)">U.S. Bank Building</a> in <a href="/wiki/Davenport,_Iowa" title="Davenport, Iowa">Davenport, Iowa</a></li>
<li>U.S. Bank Building in <a href="/wiki/Duluth,_Minnesota" title="Duluth, Minnesota">Duluth, Minnesota</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/US_Bancorp_Center" title="US Bancorp Center">U.S. Bancorp Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis,_Minnesota" class="mw-redirect" title="Minneapolis, Minnesota">Minneapolis, Minnesota</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Plaza_(Minneapolis)" title="U.S. Bank Plaza (Minneapolis)">U.S. Bank Plaza</a> in <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis,_Minnesota" class="mw-redirect" title="Minneapolis, Minnesota">Minneapolis, Minnesota</a></li>
<li>U.S. Bank Center in <a href="/wiki/St._Paul,_Minnesota" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Paul, Minnesota">St. Paul, Minnesota</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=One_U.S._Bank_Plaza&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="One U.S. Bank Plaza (page does not exist)">One U.S. Bank Plaza</a> in <a href="/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis, Missouri">St. Louis, Missouri</a></li>
<li>U.S. Bank Building in <a href="/wiki/Billings,_Montana" title="Billings, Montana">Billings, Montana</a></li>
<li>U.S. Bank Tower in <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_Nebraska" title="Lincoln, Nebraska">Lincoln, Nebraska</a></li>
<li>U.S. Bank Center in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas, Nevada</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Arena" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Bank Arena">U.S. Bank Arena</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati,_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="Cincinnati, Ohio">Cincinnati, Ohio</a></li>
<li>U.S. Bank Tower in <a href="/wiki/Cincinnati,_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="Cincinnati, Ohio">Cincinnati, Ohio</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Bank_Centre_-_Cleveland&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="U.S. Bank Centre - Cleveland (page does not exist)">U.S. Bank Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cleveland,_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="Cleveland, Ohio">Cleveland, Ohio</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/U.S._Bancorp_Tower" title="U.S. Bancorp Tower">U.S. Bancorp Tower</a> in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Building_(Sioux_Falls)" title="U.S. Bank Building (Sioux Falls)">U.S. Bank Building</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sioux_Falls,_South_Dakota" title="Sioux Falls, South Dakota">Sioux Falls, South Dakota</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Centre" title="U.S. Bank Centre">U.S. Bank Centre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle, Washington</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Old_National_Bank_Building" title="Old National Bank Building"> U.S. Bank Building</a> in <a href="/wiki/Spokane,_Washington" title="Spokane, Washington">Spokane, Washington</a></li>
<li>U.S. Bank Building in <a href="/wiki/La_Crosse,_Wisconsin" title="La Crosse, Wisconsin">La Crosse, Wisconsin</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/US_Bank_Center_(Milwaukee)" class="mw-redirect" title="US Bank Center (Milwaukee)">U.S. Bank Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee,_Wisconsin" class="mw-redirect" title="Milwaukee, Wisconsin">Milwaukee, Wisconsin</a></li>
<li>U.S. Bank Plaza in <a href="/wiki/Madison,_Wisconsin" title="Madison, Wisconsin">Madison, Wisconsin</a></li></ul></div>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Naming_rights_and_Sponsorships">Naming rights and Sponsorships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=U.S._Bancorp&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Naming rights and Sponsorships" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<p>U.S. Bank owns corporate <a href="/wiki/Naming_rights" title="Naming rights">naming rights</a> to the following:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/U.S._Bank_Stadium" title="U.S. Bank Stadium">U.S. Bank Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis,_Minnesota" class="mw-redirect" title="Minneapolis, Minnesota">Minneapolis, Minnesota</a></li></ul><p>U.S. Bank is a sponsor of:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a> - Official Bank of the Denver Broncos.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Vikings" title="Minnesota Vikings">Minnesota Vikings</a> - Official Bank of the Minnesota Vikings.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a> - Official Bank of the San Francisco 49ers.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Utah_Jazz" title="Utah Jazz">Utah Jazz</a> - Official Bank of the Utah Jazz.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/NHL" class="mw-redirect" title="NHL">NHL</a> - Official Partner of the NHL.</li></ul></div>

<li id="cite_note-wsj-1968sep09-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-wsj-1968sep09_9-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20170913230902/https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/djreprints/doc/133266993.html">"U.S. National, Oregon, Board Votes Reorganization Plan"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i>. September 9, 1968. p. 13. Archived from <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/djreprints/doc/133266993.html">the original</a></span> on September 13, 2017<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">July 7,</span> 2017</span>. <q>Directors of U.S. National Bank of Oregon approved plans to make the bank the subsidiary of a new one-bank holding company, tentatively to be called U.S. Bancorp, U.S. National announced... The move, according to LeRoy B. Staver, would permit the bank to diversify within the financial field. He added that definite plans for acquisitions haven't been formulated yet.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Wall+Street+Journal&amp;rft.atitle=U.S.+National%2C+Oregon%2C+Board+Votes+Reorganization+Plan&amp;rft.pages=13&amp;rft.date=1968-09-09&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fpqasb.pqarchiver.com%2Fdjreprints%2Fdoc%2F133266993.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://search.proquest.com/docview/133266993/">Alternate Link</a> via ProQuest.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-wsj-1968nov29-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-wsj-1968nov29_10-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20170819144432/https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/djreprints/doc/133266985.html">"Two Major Banks Get Permission to Organize One-Unit Holding Firms: Currency Comptroller Approves Three Other Such Proposals, Putting Week's Total at Seven"</a>. <i>The Wall Street Journal</i>. November 29, 1968. p. 6. Archived from <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://pqasb.pqarchiver.com/djreprints/doc/133266985.html">the original</a></span> on August 19, 2017<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">July 7,</span> 2017</span>. <q>U.S. National Bank of Portland, Ore., received permission to merge with Unit National Bank Of Oregon, currently organizing; the new institution would be owned by U.S. Bancorp. U.S. National has deposits of $1.16 billion and operates 110 offices. American Fletcher National Bank &amp; Trust Co., Indianapolis, with deposits of $594 million and 41 branches, was given approval to merge with Marion County National Bank, currently organizing. American Fletcher is owned by American Fletcher Corp.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Wall+Street+Journal&amp;rft.atitle=Two+Major+Banks+Get+Permission+to+Organize+One-Unit+Holding+Firms%3A+Currency+Comptroller+Approves+Three+Other+Such+Proposals%2C+Putting+Week%27s+Total+at+Seven&amp;rft.pages=6&amp;rft.date=1968-11-29&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fpqasb.pqarchiver.com%2Fdjreprints%2Fdoc%2F133266985.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://search.proquest.com/docview/133266985/">Alternate Link</a> via ProQuest.</span>

A letter of intent has been signed to acquire the Bank of Loleta, a state-chartered bank with assets of $143 million with seven branches in Humboldt and Del Norte counties. Purchase price is about $15.3 million in cash, the Portland-based bank holding company said... The expansion policy of U.S. Bancorp in recent years has created the third-largest bank in Washington with Old National Bancorporation of Spokane and Peoples Bancorporation of Seattle combined into U.S. Bank of Washington. Another subsidiary is U.S. Bank of Southwest Washington, based in Vancouver, and including Heritage Bank of Camas. Pending acquisitions include Mt Baker Bank, a savings bank in Bellingham, and Northwestern Commercial Bank, also in Bellingham. Last year, it also acquired Valley National Bank of Forest Grove to add to the statewide network of U.S. National Bank of Oregon.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Oregonian&amp;rft.atitle=U.S.+Bancorp+to+Expand+to+California&amp;rft.pages=E01&amp;rft.date=1988-04-09&amp;rft.aulast=Sorensen&amp;rft.aufirst=Donald+J.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnl.newsbank.com%2Fnl-search%2Fwe%2FArchives%3Fp_product%3DOR%26p_theme%3Dor%26p_action%3Dsearch%26p_maxdocs%3D200%26p_topdoc%3D1%26p_text_direct-0%3D0EB084EAE5DB2D22%26p_field_direct-0%3Ddocument_id%26p_perpage%3D10%26p_sort%3DYMD_date%3AD%26s_trackval%3DGooglePM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

<li id="cite_note-spi-1988jul23-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-spi-1988jul23_32-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=SPIB&amp;p_theme=realcities&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=0EB048EB25FF5B5F&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"U.S. Bancorp – Western Independent Bancshares Is Purchased"</a></span>. <i>Seattle Post-Intelligencer</i>. July 23, 1988. p. B3. <q>U.S. Bancorp, the Portland-based financial services company, will buy Western Independent Bancshares Inc. in Auburn for $4.25 million in cash under the terms of a definitive agreement announced yesterday. Western Independent Bancshares is the parent company of Auburn Valley Bank, which had year-end assets of $44.6 million and offices in Auburn and Kent. The previously announced acquisition, which requires the approval of Western Independent Bancshares shareholders and regulators, is one of several pending or completed by U.S. Bancorp this year. The company completed the acquisition of Mt Baker Bank in Bellingham last month, and has agreements to purchase Northwestern Commercial Bank, also in Bellingham, and the Bank of Loleta in Eureka, Calif.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Seattle+Post-Intelligencer&amp;rft.atitle=U.S.+Bancorp+%E2%80%93+Western+Independent+Bancshares+Is+Purchased&amp;rft.pages=B3&amp;rft.date=1988-07-23&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnl.newsbank.com%2Fnl-search%2Fwe%2FArchives%3Fp_product%3DSPIB%26p_theme%3Drealcities%26p_action%3Dsearch%26p_maxdocs%3D200%26p_topdoc%3D1%26p_text_direct-0%3D0EB048EB25FF5B5F%26p_field_direct-0%3Ddocument_id%26p_perpage%3D10%26p_sort%3DYMD_date%3AD%26s_trackval%3DGooglePM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
