<li id="cite_note-to-1989oct19-33"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-to-1989oct19_33-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Sorensen, Donald J. (October 19, 1989). <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=OR&amp;p_theme=or&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=0EB085B98B84F6E5&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"U.S. Bancorp Buys Women-Founded Sacramento Bank"</a></span>. <i>The Oregonian</i>. p. E17. <q>U.S. Bancorp continued its expansion into Northern California by announcing Wednesday that it has agreed to acquire Mother Lode Savings Bank of Sacramento for about $5.3 million. Mother Lode, which has assets of $107.7 million and three offices, was founded by women in 1980 as a savings and loan to encourage business development by women in the area. It was later changed to a savings bank and expanded its operations... It is one of the first acquisitions of a thrift by a commercial bank in the nation since legislation permitting such takeovers. However, the savings bank is healthy and it was not a rescue effort, U.S. Bancorp said... When the transaction is completed, expected early next year, the bank will become part of U.S. Bank of California, a Bancorp subsidiary. The California unit was formed early last year with the acquisition of the $143 million-in-assets Bank of Loleta in Eureka, Calif.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Oregonian&amp;rft.atitle=U.S.+Bancorp+Buys+Women-Founded+Sacramento+Bank&amp;rft.pages=E17&amp;rft.date=1989-10-19&amp;rft.aulast=Sorensen&amp;rft.aufirst=Donald+J.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnl.newsbank.com%2Fnl-search%2Fwe%2FArchives%3Fp_product%3DOR%26p_theme%3Dor%26p_action%3Dsearch%26p_maxdocs%3D200%26p_topdoc%3D1%26p_text_direct-0%3D0EB085B98B84F6E5%26p_field_direct-0%3Ddocument_id%26p_perpage%3D10%26p_sort%3DYMD_date%3AD%26s_trackval%3DGooglePM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

<li id="cite_note-to-1990aug26-34"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-to-1990aug26_34-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">MacKenzie, Bill (August 26, 1990). <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=OR&amp;p_theme=or&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=0EB086233915D52F&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"U.S. Bank Acquires Mother Lode Savings"</a></span>. <i>The Oregonian</i>. p. B06. <q>U.S. Bank has completed its acquisition of Mother Lode Savings Bank of Sacramento, further solidifying the Oregon bank's position in Northern California. <li id="cite_note-sfc-1991jul29-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-sfc-1991jul29_35-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Howe, Kenneth (July 29, 1991). <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=SFCB&amp;p_theme=sfcb&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=0EB4F37CF634AAA3&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"U.S. Bancorp on Northern California Buying Spree"</a></span>. <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i>. p. B1. <q>U.S. Bancorp, with $18.6 billion in assets, is the country's 35th biggest bank. Breezley's goal is to get it among the top 20 banks by 1994. Even if the bigger banks were to stop growing, U.S. Bancorp would have to expand by 70 percent over the next 3 1/2 years to achieve the goal. But that may not be as difficult as it sounds. The company has tripled in size since 1983... Started from scratch 2 1/2 years ago, the company's U.S. Bank of California unit, with about $1.4 billion in assets, already is the seventh-largest bank headquartered in Northern California. Forming U.S. Bank of California after buying the tiny Bank of Loleta in Eureka at the end of 1988, Breezley added Sacramento's Mother Lode Savings in 1990 and Auburn's HeartFed Financial Corp. and Petaluma's Northbay Financial this year... Much of U.S. Bancorp's growth has occurred in the state of Washington, where the company has made six acquisitions in four years and where U.S. Bank of Washington, with $5.4 billion in assets, is now the third-largest bank. Breezley's next target is Idaho, where his blend of caution and aggression is evident. Tejera said that last year U.S. Bancorp tried three times to buy Idaho institutions: First National Bank of North Idaho in Wallace, Mountain West Savings Bank of Coeur d'Alene and Boise-based West One Bancorp. "They played it very conservative in those attempts, walking away when the price got too steep," he said.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=San+Francisco+Chronicle&amp;rft.atitle=U.S.+Bancorp+on+Northern+California+Buying+Spree&amp;rft.pages=B1&amp;rft.date=1991-07-29&amp;rft.aulast=Howe&amp;rft.aufirst=Kenneth&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnl.newsbank.com%2Fnl-search%2Fwe%2FArchives%3Fp_product%3DSFCB%26p_theme%3Dsfcb%26p_action%3Dsearch%26p_maxdocs%3D200%26p_topdoc%3D1%26p_text_direct-0%3D0EB4F37CF634AAA3%26p_field_direct-0%3Ddocument_id%26p_perpage%3D10%26p_sort%3DYMD_date%3AD%26s_trackval%3DGooglePM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-prn-1994jan06-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-prn-1994jan06_46-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation pressrelease"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.thefreelibrary.com/GERRY+B.+CAMERON+NAMED+CHIEF+OPERATING+OFFICER+OF+U.S.+BANCORP-a014679274">"Gerry B. Cameron Named Chief Operating Officer Of U.S. Bancorp"</a> (Press release). U.S. Bancorp. January 6, 1994 – via <a href="/wiki/The_Free_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="The Free Library">The Free Library</a>. <q>Chairman Roger L. Breezley today announced that the board of directors of U.S. Bancorp has elected Vice Chairman Gerry Cameron to the additional position of chief operating officer (COO). With the new position, Cameron's scope of responsibility broadens from his traditional regional banking focus to include oversight of nationally focused financial businesses. Cameron assumes the title previously held by Edmund P. Jensen who recently left U.S. Bancorp to join Visa International as president and chief executive officer. Kevin R. Kelly remains as president of U.S. Bancorp.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Gerry+B.+Cameron+Named+Chief+Operating+Officer+Of+U.S.+Bancorp&amp;rft.pub=U.S.+Bancorp&amp;rft.date=1994-01-06&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.thefreelibrary.com%2FGERRY%2BB.%2BCAMERON%2BNAMED%2BCHIEF%2BOPERATING%2BOFFICER%2BOF%2BU.S.%2BBANCORP-a014679274&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

<li id="cite_note-to-1994jan27-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-to-1994jan27_47-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Francis, Mike &amp; Hamburg, Ken (January 27, 1994). <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=OR&amp;p_theme=or&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=0EB08839B2C0C135&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"U.S. Bancorp Board Puts Cameron In Charge"</a></span>. <i>The Oregonian</i>. p. C01. <q>The directors of U.S. Bancorp put a new man in charge Wednesday, ending speculation about the succession at the region's largest independent bank. Gerry Cameron, a 38-year veteran of U.S. Bancorp, was named chief executive officer of the regional holding company. He succeeds Roger Breezley, who remains chairman of the company, a position he has held since 1987. Breezley, 55, surrendered his day-to-day management duties at the bank. The leadership change -- effective immediately -- was announced Wednesday night following an afternoon meeting of the company's directors. A statement by Breezley said he had recommended that the functions of chairman and chief executive be split. The change, he said, allows him to focus on oversight. The suddenness of the change surprised even bank insiders. About an hour after the directors adjourned, the senior vice president for investor relations said he hadn't heard about the change.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Oregonian&amp;rft.atitle=U.S.+Bancorp+Board+Puts+Cameron+In+Charge&amp;rft.pages=C01&amp;rft.date=1994-01-27&amp;rft.aulast=Francis&amp;rft.aufirst=Mike&amp;rft.au=Hamburg%2C+Ken&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnl.newsbank.com%2Fnl-search%2Fwe%2FArchives%3Fp_product%3DOR%26p_theme%3Dor%26p_action%3Dsearch%26p_maxdocs%3D200%26p_topdoc%3D1%26p_text_direct-0%3D0EB08839B2C0C135%26p_field_direct-0%3Ddocument_id%26p_perpage%3D10%26p_sort%3DYMD_date%3AD%26s_trackval%3DGooglePM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

<li id="cite_note-to-1994mar19-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-to-1994mar19_48-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Francis, Mike (March 19, 1994). <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=OR&amp;p_theme=or&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=0EB08846C0F538CC&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"Kelly Steps Down at U.S. Bancorp"</a></span>. <i>The Oregonian</i>. p. E01. <q>Kevin R. <li id="cite_note-nyt-1994apr20-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-nyt-1994apr20_49-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.nytimes.com/1994/04/20/business/company-news-chairman-of-us-bancorp-steps-down.html?pagewanted=all">"Chairman Of U.S. Bancorp Steps Down"</a></span>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i>. The company, based in Portland, Ore., also said it planned to buy back up to six million shares to finance the company's 1993 stock incentive plan and for other corporate purposes. The company has about 99.7 million shares outstanding. Mr. Breezley, 56, will remain on the board. He relinquished the chief executive's post in January, the company said.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+New+York+Times&amp;rft.atitle=Chairman+Of+U.S.+Bancorp+Steps+Down&amp;rft.date=1994-04-20&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nytimes.com%2F1994%2F04%2F20%2Fbusiness%2Fcompany-news-chairman-of-us-bancorp-steps-down.html%3Fpagewanted%3Dall&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

<li id="cite_note-to-1995may09-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-to-1995may09_52-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Manning, Jeff (May 9, 1995). <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=OR&amp;p_theme=or&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=0EB088EE28C83E04&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"Banking on Bigness: U.S. Buying West One"</a></span>. <i>The Oregonian]</i>. p. A01. <q>U.S. Bancorp announced Monday morning its intention to buy Boise-based West One Bancorp in a deal valued at $1.6 billion. The acquisition would boost U.S. Bancorp's total assets from $21.4 billion to more than $30 billion, solidifying its position as the largest Northwest-owned bank... The merger cements U.S. Bancorp's position as the largest bank in Oregon. It also will become the largest institution in Idaho and move from fifth-largest to third-largest in Washington. West One also gives U.S. Bancorp its first entry into Utah. The acquisition probably will raise antitrust concerns among Justice Department lawyers. U.S. Bancorp acknowledged that it probably will have to divest assets in certain markets, especially the Portland metropolitan area, to gain government approval... The acquisition clears up speculation about who U.S. Bancorp's next chief executive will be. As part of the deal, the Portland bank named West One's chairman and chief executive, Dan Nelson, its own chief operating officer and president. What's more, Nelson will assume the bank's helm after Cameron retires in three years.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Oregonian%5D&amp;rft.atitle=Banking+on+Bigness%3A+U.S.+Buying+West+One&amp;rft.pages=A01&amp;rft.date=1995-05-09&amp;rft.aulast=Manning&amp;rft.aufirst=Jeff&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnl.newsbank.com%2Fnl-search%2Fwe%2FArchives%3Fp_product%3DOR%26p_theme%3Dor%26p_action%3Dsearch%26p_maxdocs%3D200%26p_topdoc%3D1%26p_text_direct-0%3D0EB088EE28C83E04%26p_field_direct-0%3Ddocument_id%26p_perpage%3D10%26p_sort%3DYMD_date%3AD%26s_trackval%3DGooglePM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

January 4, 1997. p. E10. <q>U.S. Bank has finalized its acquisition of St. George-based Sun Capital Bank in a deal valued at $15.5 million. Under terms of an agreement originally signed Sept. 25, two Sun Capital branches in St. George and one in Hurricane will merge this spring into U.S. Bank... The merger will bring to 29 the number of U.S. Bank branches operating in Utah. The bank with $33 billion in assets moved into the state in April through its acquisition of West One Bank.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Salt+Lake+Tribune&amp;rft.atitle=Meanwhile+in+Utah+...&amp;rft.pages=E10&amp;rft.date=1997-01-04&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnl.newsbank.com%2Fnl-search%2Fwe%2FArchives%3Fp_product%3DSLTB%26p_theme%3Dsltb%26p_action%3Dsearch%26p_maxdocs%3D200%26p_topdoc%3D1%26p_text_direct-0%3D100F80DAE33E75A5%26p_field_direct-0%3Ddocument_id%26p_perpage%3D10%26p_sort%3DYMD_date%3AD%26s_trackval%3DGooglePM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

<li id="cite_note-mst-1997aug02-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-mst-1997aug02_67-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">DePass, Dee (August 2, 1997). <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=MN&amp;p_theme=mn&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=0EFD61F58BB6DD78&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"It's a done deal: First Bank System acquires U.S. Bancorp – and its name – Analysts are waiting to see whether new combined company will make planned $340 million in expense cuts by next year"</a></span>. <i><a href="/wiki/Minneapolis_Star-Tribune" class="mw-redirect" title="Minneapolis Star-Tribune">Minneapolis Star-Tribune</a></i>. p. 02D. <q>First Bank System closed on its acquisition of Portland, Ore.-based U.S. Bancorp. Friday and changed its name to U.S. Bancorp. The new combined company will be headquartered in Minneapolis. The deal creates a robust financial institution operating in 17 states with $72 billion in assets and a market capitalization of $22 billion. It becomes the 14th-largest bank holding company in the country based on assets, and the 10th-largest based on market capitalization. Effective Monday, the ticker symbol will change to USB and the stock will trade on the New York Stock Exchange. "While this is a defining moment in the history of First Bank System as a bank holding company, it will be business as usual for customers at all our bank branches for the immediate future," said John F. Grundhofer, who will serve as president and chief executive officer of the new U.S. Bancorp.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Minneapolis+Star-Tribune&amp;rft.atitle=It%27s+a+done+deal%3A+First+Bank+System+acquires+U.S.+Bancorp+%E2%80%93+and+its+name+%E2%80%93+Analysts+are+waiting+to+see+whether+new+combined+company+will+make+planned+%24340+million+in+expense+cuts+by+next+year&amp;rft.pages=02D&amp;rft.date=1997-08-02&amp;rft.aulast=DePass&amp;rft.aufirst=Dee&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnl.newsbank.com%2Fnl-search%2Fwe%2FArchives%3Fp_product%3DMN%26p_theme%3Dmn%26p_action%3Dsearch%26p_maxdocs%3D200%26p_topdoc%3D1%26p_text_direct-0%3D0EFD61F58BB6DD78%26p_field_direct-0%3Ddocument_id%26p_perpage%3D10%26p_sort%3DYMD_date%3AD%26s_trackval%3DGooglePM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

Rosenberg, a bank auditor, was one of several hundred Portland workers laid off Friday, hours after Minneapolis-based First Bank System Inc. completed its $9.9 billion stock-swap takeover of the old U.S. Bancorp. Both companies won approval from stockholders Thursday to merge. The combined company wasted no time launching a reorganization that will eliminate 4,000 jobs in 18 months. More than half the cuts will be in the Portland area... First Bank System Inc. of Minneapolis adopted the U.S. Bancorp name Friday. The new U.S. Bancorp began its first day of business assuring customers that they would see no changes in their customer accounts for a while. <li id="cite_note-sppp-1998dec24-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-sppp-1998dec24_75-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">Huber, Tim (December 24, 1998). <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=SP&amp;p_theme=realcities2&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=0EB5E36B0A6BCDD3&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"Cameron to Step Down at Bancorp"</a></span>. <i>St. Paul Pioneer Press</i>. p. 3B. <q>Minneapolis-based U.S. Bancorp said Wednesday that chairman Gerry Cameron would retire at the end of the year as planned. He will be succeeded by U.S. Bancorp president and chief executive John Grundhofer. Cameron was chief executive of Portland, Ore.-based U.S. Bancorp when it was acquired for $9 billion by Minneapolis-based First Bank System Inc. First Bank assumed the U.S. Bancorp name when the deal closed in March. Cameron became chairman of the merged company. The move is not a surprise. <li id="cite_note-mst-1998dec29-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-mst-1998dec29_76-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">DePass, Dee (December 29, 1998). <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=MN&amp;p_theme=mn&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=0EFD64E98B861AC3&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"Grundhofer gains title as U.S. Bancorp chair retires – Cameron steps down after 40-year career"</a></span>. <i>Minneapolis Star-Tribune</i>. p. 01D. <q>U.S. Bancorp Chairman Gerry Cameron will retire effective Thursday, ending a banking career that spanned four decades. Cameron in 1997 had announced his intention to retire by the end of this year, so the move is no surprise. But it does further cement the passing of control at the old U.S. Bancorp, where Cameron was the CEO and president before the August 1997 sale of the Portland-based bank to Minneapolis-based First Bank System. After the deal closed, First Bank took the U.S. Bancorp name. Cameron's departure gives John (Jack) Grundhofer the title of chairman in addition to chief executive and president. Cameron remained out West after the acquisition, which caused many analysts to believe he had effectively given up control of the company long before his official Dec. 31 retirement.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Minneapolis+Star-Tribune&amp;rft.atitle=Grundhofer+gains+title+as+U.S.+Bancorp+chair+retires+%E2%80%93+Cameron+steps+down+after+40-year+career&amp;rft.pages=01D&amp;rft.date=1998-12-29&amp;rft.aulast=DePass&amp;rft.aufirst=Dee&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnl.newsbank.com%2Fnl-search%2Fwe%2FArchives%3Fp_product%3DMN%26p_theme%3Dmn%26p_action%3Dsearch%26p_maxdocs%3D200%26p_topdoc%3D1%26p_text_direct-0%3D0EFD64E98B861AC3%26p_field_direct-0%3Ddocument_id%26p_perpage%3D10%26p_sort%3DYMD_date%3AD%26s_trackval%3DGooglePM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

(January 7, 2000). <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=SDUB&amp;p_theme=sdub&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=116D30D6C423DEA3&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"Peninsula Bank shareholders move to block merger"</a></span>. <i>San Diego Union Tribune</i>. pp. C-1. <q>A group of shareholders in Peninsula Bank of San Diego has moved to thwart Peninsula's merger with U.S. Bancorp, arguing the $100 million deal was "materially altered" when U.S. Bancorp cut its earnings estimate... Peninsula said last September that the bank had agreed to a buyout proposal submitted by Minneapolis-based U.S. Bancorp, the nation's No. 12 bank. The deal was valued then at approximately $100 million to $120 million. But the lawsuit is focused on a subsequent announcement issued Dec. 6, when U.S. Bancorp said lower-than-expected revenue and increased investments had reduced earnings expectations for the fourth quarter and the rest of 2000. The news sent shares of U.S. Bancorp plummeting by more than 27 percent that day, erasing more than $7 billion of market value. Before U.S. Bancorp's disclosure, the Minnesota bank had an estimated 12 percent rate in its earnings growth. The actual rate is now closer to 5 percent, Robbins said.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=San+Diego+Union+Tribune&amp;rft.atitle=Peninsula+Bank+shareholders+move+to+block+merger&amp;rft.pages=C-1&amp;rft.date=2000-01-07&amp;rft.aulast=Bigelow&amp;rft.aufirst=Bruce+V.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnl.newsbank.com%2Fnl-search%2Fwe%2FArchives%3Fp_product%3DSDUB%26p_theme%3Dsdub%26p_action%3Dsearch%26p_maxdocs%3D200%26p_topdoc%3D1%26p_text_direct-0%3D116D30D6C423DEA3%26p_field_direct-0%3Ddocument_id%26p_perpage%3D10%26p_sort%3DYMD_date%3AD%26s_trackval%3DGooglePM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>

<li id="cite_note-mst-2001feb27-100"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-mst-2001feb27_100-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">DePass, Dee (February 27, 2001). <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=MN&amp;p_theme=mn&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=0EFCD2744B76E870&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"USB, Firstar make it official – Many Firstar executives moving to the Minneapolis headquarters"</a></span>. <i>Minneapolis Star-Tribune</i>. p. 01D. <q>Firstar Corp. completes its $22 billion acquisition of U.S. Bancorp today, creating the nation's eighth-largest bank and triggering a move by a number of Firstar executives from Milwaukee to Minnesota. The influx of more than a dozen top Firstar personnel is expected to take place over the next few months. The headquarters of the combined bank will be in Minneapolis and the combined firm will keep the U.S. Bancorp name. Firstar CEO Jerry Grundhofer becomes CEO of the new, $160 billion U.S. Bancorp. Grundhofer, who replaces his older brother, Jack, in the role of USB CEO, reportedly already has located property in the Twin Cities and expects to move here by the fall. Jack Grundhofer becomes chairman of the combined organization. He will retire next year... The bank will be based in Minneapolis, retain the U.S. Bancorp name and span 24 states with nearly 2,200 branches. The bank will have $107 billion in deposits and 51,000 employees. (Firstar had 23,000, USB 28,000.) The combined bank plans to cut $266 million in expenses over three years, but few layoffs are planned because there was little geographic overlap between the banks. The New CEO will be former Firstar CEO Jerry Grundhofer. Former USB CEO John Grundhofer will be the chairman and retire in 2002.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Minneapolis+Star-Tribune&amp;rft.atitle=USB%2C+Firstar+make+it+official+%E2%80%93+Many+Firstar+executives+moving+to+the+Minneapolis+headquarters&amp;rft.pages=01D&amp;rft.date=2001-02-27&amp;rft.aulast=DePass&amp;rft.aufirst=Dee&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnl.newsbank.com%2Fnl-search%2Fwe%2FArchives%3Fp_product%3DMN%26p_theme%3Dmn%26p_action%3Dsearch%26p_maxdocs%3D200%26p_topdoc%3D1%26p_text_direct-0%3D0EFCD2744B76E870%26p_field_direct-0%3Ddocument_id%26p_perpage%3D10%26p_sort%3DYMD_date%3AD%26s_trackval%3DGooglePM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-mst-2001feb01-103"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-mst-2001feb01_103-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">DePass, Dee (February 1, 2001). <span class="cs1-lock-subscription" title="Paid subscription required"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nl.newsbank.com/nl-search/we/Archives?p_product=MN&amp;p_theme=mn&amp;p_action=search&amp;p_maxdocs=200&amp;p_topdoc=1&amp;p_text_direct-0=0EFCD217633CAECD&amp;p_field_direct-0=document_id&amp;p_perpage=10&amp;p_sort=YMD_date:D&amp;s_trackval=GooglePM">"Firstar to sell 11 branches to Bremer Bank"</a></span>. <i>Minneapolis Star-Tribune</i>. p. 01D. <q>Milwaukee-based Firstar Corp. will sell 11 of its branches to Bremer Bank in St. Paul to comply with market-share rules governing its pending purchase of U.S. Bancorp. The branches are all in the Twin Cities and represent $760 million in deposits, about one-third of Firstar's current Minnesota franchise. The combined U.S. Bancorp-Firstar will have 90 branches in the Twin Cities after the divestiture, scheduled to take place in June.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Minneapolis+Star-Tribune&amp;rft.atitle=Firstar+to+sell+11+branches+to+Bremer+Bank&amp;rft.pages=01D&amp;rft.date=2001-02-01&amp;rft.aulast=DePass&amp;rft.aufirst=Dee&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fnl.newsbank.com%2Fnl-search%2Fwe%2FArchives%3Fp_product%3DMN%26p_theme%3Dmn%26p_action%3Dsearch%26p_maxdocs%3D200%26p_topdoc%3D1%26p_text_direct-0%3D0EFCD217633CAECD%26p_field_direct-0%3Ddocument_id%26p_perpage%3D10%26p_sort%3DYMD_date%3AD%26s_trackval%3DGooglePM&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AU.S.+Bancorp" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
